text:
I lost my Gran's recipe & was so happy 2 find the same one here! The recipe tastes great as written but over the years I've made a few changes(according to my personal taste)and with a few small adjustments, I prefer it. So, I thought I'd share. Firstly, instead of white sugar, I use 1/2 C packed brown sugar. The molasses in the brown sugar makes this pudding taste richer. The original recipe calls for 3 Tbs cocoa, I heap my Tbs to make it a bit more chocolately. I also find 1/4 C cornstarch was a little too much for me, as the pudding went as firm as jello the next day instead of staying creamy. If u add just over half that amount & cook it slightly longer it gels less. Of course, if you like it that way or are using this recipe to make a chocolate pie or square that you want to keep it's shape when cut, then you'll want to use the full amount. Lastly, I always use evaporated milk when cooking. It just tastes creamier to me. Thanks for posting this recipe, Kelly! Update,July 09: To avoid lumps, put 1st 4 ingredients in saucepan and mix well. If there are any lumps, get in there with your fingers and work them out. If you don't want to do it with your hands you can use a sifter or push them through a sieve. You must have a smooth, lump-free powder before you add your liquid. I also use a whisk and constantly stir. Lastly, it will sometimes thicken before it boils but I find if I don't let it boil for even just 10 seconds, I can taste the cornstarch in it. Thanks :)

text:
Very very easy pudding. I also used three 'heaping' teaspoons of the cocoa, since I really enjoy a nice deep chocolate flavor. Make sure not to overcook, and never boil or it tends to try and lump up on you, but that can be resolved with a brisk whisking as the mixture starts to cool. Another tip is when you put it in the fridge to cool completly, try to make sure you have brought it down to about lukewarm temperature outside the fridge, I whisk away at it while having the sink filled about an inch or two deep with cold water and some ice cubes, really cuts down on the wait time for that. AND when you finally do put it in the fridge, use some plastic wrap to cover but make sure the plastic is lying directly on top of the pudding, actually touching it all the way over the top. This seems to prevent that top layer of strange congealed pudding you sometimes get when the pudding sits for awhile,which taste fine, but is a bit odd compared to the creamy pudding underneath it.

My daughter Kelly submitted this (my) recipe a number of years ago...this is still my favorite, after all these years. I've been reading some of the reviews. I now make this recipe with only 1/3 Cup of white sugar. I also heap the cocoa measurements. Also, after cooling a bit, place plastic wrap right down over the top of the pudding and this prevents the rubbery film from forming.  DO NOT REDUCE THE CORNSTARCH MEASUREMENT.If it's too think you're over cooking it, if it's too thin...you're under cooking. I've found this recipe to be virtually fool proof. ENJOY!!

text:
Good, basic pudding recipe.  Here's tip for unexperienced pudding makers: don't stir constantly until the milk starts to boil.  I used to stir the milk the whole time, and it would take FOREVER to boil and the milk would sometimes get a burnt flavor because it was on the heat for so long.  Only stir occasionally until it starts to boil (otherwise it keeps losing the heat and won't get hot enough to boil), and then stir constantly for about 2-3 minutes before taking it off the heat.  If you do that, then it is easy and relatively fast to make pudding.

text:
Fantastic!! I had been craving chocolate pudding for like two days and decided to make it from scratch instead of buying the boring box version.  It turned out phenomenal and I'll definitely be making this again.  As for my personal taste, I could have appreciated a little more salt but it was still very good.  One great hint: USE A DOUBLE BOILER!!!  However, when using a double boiler to make pudding: boil the water in the bottom pot on high FIRST before adding the top pot. While waiting on the bottom pot to start boiling, add all the dry ingredients to the top pot and whisk until WELL blended to get rid of any dry clumps.  Once the dry ingredients are blended, add the top pot to the pot of boiling water and then add your milk a little at a time while whisking briskly. This technique will give you a flawlessly smooth texture without any clumps AT ALL.  ENJOY!!

text:
For taste, this pudding earns five stars. Overall and as written, 4. I rounded the tablespoons of cocoa for a more chocolaty flavor and it was perfect. It wasn't bitter or that really dark, rich chocolate. Still light and creamy but just chocolaty enough. Be sure to use salted butter and add the additional salt; it really makes a difference as salt enhances chocolate. Eaten hot, the pudding's consistency isn't a problem but once it stars to cool down it firms up like gelatin. Next time I'll decrease the cornstarch. I also used butter (never margarine). For best results use a whisk for this recipe and be sure to scrape the "corners" of the saucepan constantly to avoid burning. I love how easy and delicious this was, and will totally be making it again.

text:
This was very good.  I quadrupled the recipe (large family) and used fresh, raw goat milk.  I did everything else almost exactly according to the recipe.  TIP: For those of you that found that your pudding gets grainy the next day, that's because food thickened with corn starch is meant to be heated and then eaten hot.  When it gets cold it causes the food to separate.  I used the same amount of a product called "Clear Jel" which is a modified corn starch.  I use it for home canned pie fillings as a thickener because it thickens fast and is stable at room temperature and when it's cold.  Here is what I did: I added all the dry ingredients (1/2 white, 1/2 brown sugar) to the saucepan except the Clear Jel and worked all the lumps out (I did add a bit of whole egg powder but I don't think it was necessary and I wouldn't do it again).  Next I added all the milk less 1/2 - 1 cup to the saucepan and stir well.  Then I mixed the reserved milk and Clear Jel in the Magic Bullet to get all the lumps out.  Bring the pudding mixture to a boil like the recipe calls for and once it's boiling, add the milk mixture all at once and stir rapidly.  It will thicken almost immediately to an almost "too thick" mixture.  Once I added the butter and vanilla, it was exactly the perfect texture and the texture will stay the same after it's refrigerated.  You can get Clear Jel online; it's usually available at your local co-op or extension service.

text:
Easy to adapt for diabetics to make a sugar-free treat. I have experimented with various amounts of Splenda, including 1:1, 1.5:1, and my favorite, 2:1. It always takes more Splenda than sugar, no matter what the package says. Because I love deep chocolate, I use 5 level tablespoons of Dutch process cocoa, which makes a huge difference in this recipe. Dutch process cocoa has been alkalized, which neutralizes the acidity that is present in non-alkalized cocoa, such as Hershey's, the most readily available brand in the US. It costs more to buy Dutch process cocoa, but it's money well spent. I buy it in bulk online and use it in everything that calls for cocoa, such as hot chocolate, cakes, and cookies. However, since I have added a full 2 Tb beyond what is called for in the recipe, I believe that's at least part of why it takes so much more Splenda. I've learned to streamline the process by cooking it in the microwave. Give it 3 minutes at full power initially, then whisk well, and set for increments of 1 minute, whisking well after each minute until it reaches the consistency you like, remembering that additional thickening occurs after refrigeration. For me, in my 1000 watt microwave, I only need one additional minute, but bear in mind that your mileage may vary. Add the butter and vanilla, whisk one last time, pour into serving dishes and chill. About 7-8 minutes, start-to-finish. Great depth of chocolate flavor. Simple, satisfying comfort food.

I gave this 4 stars just because I think the amount of cornstarch is way more than is necessary and there needs to be more cocoa.  I tweaked my pudding using flour instead of cornstarch (substitution is 1 tbsp cornstarch equals 2 tbsp flour)and 1/4 cup cornstarch is 4 tbsp   so you would -according to this recipe- need 8 tbsp flour or 1/2 cup.  I only used about 5 tbsp and the consistency was PERFECT once it chilled.  I also added about 4 tbsp cocoa give or take (I didn't measure accurately) as well as a hint of cinnamon.  I was wanting cinnamon chocolate :). Cook it till it looks like a really thick soup and chill before eating.  I personally do NOT like warm puddings unless its bread pudding.  Very quick and easy pudding with just things you have on hand!  Good eats!

text:
Great basic recipe, but it was too thick, too sweet, and not quite chocolatey enough for my personal tastes.  I tweaked it to just 1/4 cup maple sugar, 1/2 cup dutch processed cocoa, and 3 Tbsp corn starch in 3 cups of skim milk.  I whisked the dry ingredients first to make sure no lumps, and added the milk gradually while whisking so everything was fully incorporated before putting on the heat.  It took about 10 minutes on medium heat to reach a low boil, and I kept it simmering while I stirred for another 3 minutes or so.  Perfect texture and taste for me.  Thank you so much for such a great, easy recipe!

Great recipe! I just mix everything in the pan on the counter, not over heat, and when cook it, the heat is medium-high (but, hey, it's just me). For those who made it and it came out soupy, cook it until it's really, REALLY thick, almost lumpy. Trust me, I've made it for a while now, and the last few tries it has become soupy, but I just made it two days ago, and making it so thick it's kinda lumpy makes it. Have ALL faith in my suggestion, because it will come out smooth (when you eat it).

text:
Wow!  I haven't made homemade chocolate pudding in a long time because the recipe I tried many years ago just didn't cut it.  This one, however, was spectacular!  I followed a couple of the hints from others--used rounded tablespoons of cocoa and used packed brown sugar in place of the white sugar.  I also tasted it and found it needed 1/4 tsp. salt to a single batch perfectly balance the flavors instead of 1/8 tsp.  Although I only had skim milk on hand, since it was the holidays I didn't want it to taste watered down, so I replaced 3/4 cup of skim milk with heavy cream.  Although we are not really dessert eaters, the 6 of us who had it ate a double batch! Hmmmm...maybe this is not such a good recipe after all! : )

I use three HEAPING tbs of hershey's special dark cocoa for a deep rich flavor and color. A tip - throw the sugar and cocoa in your coffee grinder and give it a buzz - it'll dissolve much more easily into the milk. Just prepare yourself to stand there and whisk till it feels like your arm is going to fall off - totally worth losing an arm though.

Can't wait to try it with other fruit like strawberries. HATS OFF TO THE LADY THAT SUBMITTED THIS RECIPIE AND HATS OFF TO HER MOTHER TOO.

This recipe is great, although I did modify it quite a bit. I used skim/fat free milk. I used 1/4 c. white sugar and 1/4 c. brown sugar. It wasn't chocolately enough, so I threw in a generous handful of semi-sweet chocolate chips right before adding the margarine & vanilla. I used only 1 tbsp. of margarine. These modifications made a fantastic, quick, and easy treat! I am a chocoholic and I found that it was actually almost too rich (despite the skim milk & 1/2 margarine) because of adding too many chocolate chips. I think next time I'll just add an extra tbsp. of cocoa and it will be perfect. As an added bonus, when you use fat free milk & only 1 tbsp margarine, it's a pretty low cal/fat treat!

Doesn't get much better than this!!  Made this recipe a few hours ago and can't wait for it to get chilled in the fridge.  I did sample it hot and it was awesome!!  The only thing I did different was kick start the cooking in the microwave.  About 2 min and stirring every 30 sec. until it started to thicken.. Did I say this chocolate pudding was awesome??  Thanks for this recipe!

text:
Delicious...NOTHING like Jello instant pudding!! It's the real thing! I heaped my tablespoons of cocoa used brown sugar instead of white, and used 1 can of evaporated milk with the balance of 2% milk. I  put the cocoa and corn starch through the sifter to remove any lumps. I used approx 1/8 cup corn starch, but should bump that up a bit next time. I stirred it constantly over medium heat JUST until boiling. Cooled the pan in ice water in the sink (stirring constantly) then transferred to a serving bowl and covered with plastic wrap "touching" the pudding to prevent the film from forming on top. Refrigerated for a few hours, dished it into individual servings and topped with whipped cream...wonderful dessert!

text:
Same recipe I've used for 40 years.  If you like it a bit thicker, you can use a bit more cornstarch.  Just a note-- if you are low on milk but have instant powdered dry milk, you can add the dry milk powder in with the sugar and other dry ingredients and just add in the water that is necessary to make up the correct amount of milk.  It doesn't hurt the taste.  This is obviously a keeper recipe.

text:
I have made this recipe several times with only two modifications.  I use almond milk since I don't drink cow's milk and I use brown sugar since I never seem to have white sugar. I got tired of always having to look the recipe up so  I finally decided to save time by mixing a large batch of the dry ingredients together so I have my own pudding mix. I altered the number of servings on the site to figure out how much of each ingredient to mix. When I am ready to make pudding I just add 2/3 cup of dry ingredients to a pot and 2 cups of milk to the pot.  This is a slightly smaller amount than the 4 serving recipe listed here.  It is about 2 cups of pudding. Works great everytime.  The leftovers are great cold but I prefer warm chocolate pudding.

text:
This was excellent!!!  I am lactose intolerant so instead of milk I tried Almond Breeze and I doubled the Hershey's cocoa because so many reviews said it needed more.  I microwaved mine in two minute increments, three times, using a wisk in between to mix the pudding, for a total of 6 minutes, then added the butter and vanilla!!  With Almond Breeze it tasted a lot like a nutty candy bar chocolate.  

I then made a batch using So Delicious Dairy Free Coconut Milk.  It seemed way too thin so I added another tablespoon of cornstarch, but whoa la at 6 minutes in the microwave it was very thick but after adding the butter and vanilla it was a very nice consistancy.  Made with the Coconut milk it seemed more like the name brand cook and serve pudding!!

Both work very well for those out there like me that are lactose intolerent!!!!  Making it another choice for a great dessert or when you really need chocolate!!!

text:
My daughter is severely allergic to milk.  I was dismayed when realized that I had accidentally grabbed the wrong box of pudding (with non-fat dry milk) at the store to make her favorite "dirt pudding".  Found this recipe and substituted soymilk and it turned out perfectly!  Passed my taste test (I don't care for soymilk) because I couldn't even tell that it wasn't made with real milk.  Stir CONSTANTLY with silicone spatula otherwise the cornstarch mixture congeals at the bottom of the saucepan.  Be patient, might take at least 10 minutes to thicken when using soymilk.

text:
This pudding tasted delicious. So surprised at how much better a from scratch pudding can be compared to the taste of a box instant mix. Will never be buying a mix again as this recipe was so easy to make that it wasn't even funny. 10 minutes MAX, and that includes prep/cooking times. Mine is in the fridge chilling right now. Although I've only made it once so far (bet your bottom dollar I'll be making it plenty of times over again) I'll just suggest one tip, when the recipe says stir constantly when it's boiling (or even slightly before then actually), STIR CONSTANTLY, the mixture sticks to the bottom of the pan easier than anything I've ever seen. You don't have to stir quickly but stir constantly as 15 seconds of not stiring can probably be disastrous. I halved the recipe as I was only making some for myself but added 1 1/2 T of extra cocoa as I like my pudding extra chocolaty but that's just to my particular taste. Also I used 2 % milk and it turned out fine.

text:
Excellent.  I made mine with skim milk and Splenda to save carbs and calories.  One recommendation is to whisk all dry ingredients in a small bowl with a couple ounces of the milk, till smooth, then add to the pot of cold milk, and whisk continuously on med heat till it just boils.  Then remove from heat and pour into serving bowls.   Cover with plastic wrap and chill if you decide not to eat warm.  If you prefer not to have a 'skin' place plastic wrap directly on the surface and when you take it off-no skin!  Enjoy!

Pretty good and turned out well.    I have scorched pudding before so I started the burner at 5 and then once the pudding was slightly thickened I turned it to 3 to thicken the rest of the way.  I also made sure to stir this pudding the entire to time cooking also to avoid scorching.  Whisking the dry ingredients with the milk well also stopped them from settling to the bottom.  At first I thought it wasn't thick enough, but after about 6 hours in the fridge it was perfect.  Plan to use in a chocolate cream pie.  Thanks for submitting!

text:
Easy, classic pudding recipe. I use almond milk to cut down on the carbs. Tip to others, make a paste with the cornstarch, cocoa, sugar/salt and cold liquid first, adding more liquid as you blend. The cornstarch and cocoa will clump up otherwise, no matter how much you blend it. THey need to be mixed into a cold liquid first.   The cocoa quality really does matter, use Dutch processed if you can. The bad reviews re: chocolate taste probably used cheap cocoa.   If I don't have cocoa on hand I'll use chocolate chips instead (added to warming pudding, stirring constantly and cut back on the sugar.

(and a 1/2)  If you're having trouble w/lumps, might I suggest the following: whisk together dry ingredients as directed. Then prior to putting on the heat, S-L-O-W-L-Y whisk in the milk... a little bit at a time (kinda like when you're making a roux). The "thick mass" thrashing around in the pot will eliminate all the lumps!

text:
This pudding is absolutely perfect, to say the least! It has a very raw chocolate taste to it, akin to the difference between store bought hot chocolate and homemade hot cocoa, this being the latter. I only had non-fat milk on hand, other than that I followed the recipe exactly. I was worried about over/under cooking it but I followed the advice of waiting till it coats a metal spoon, then cooked it a little more because it still looked runny. It does thicken upon standing, though. When I popped it in the microwave the next morning, it was as if I had just made it: still perfect. The only difference being that directly from the fridge it looked a little grainy, probably because of the non-fat milk. I have an aversion to undercooked eggs, so much so that it doesnt matter how cooked they are, the outcome has to be absolutely solid for me to eat it; the cornstarch is genius. I wont ever buy pudding again.

text:
Excellent taste and texture.  Exactly what chocolate pudding should be.  Very easy to make even for those who are recipe challenged.  To those who complained of runny pudding, here's a tip:
When cooking with cornstarch, if you must taste, use a clean spoon for each tasting.   Never put the spoon back in the pot after it has been licked.  Digestive enzymes found in your saliva will break down the cornstarch.  Incidently this is also true for Cool Whip.  Thanks Kelly.

city:
None
region:
None
country:
None
text:
This is a delicious chocolate pudding. I've been making this recipe and using frozen goat milk (since I have goats that aren't producing right now). It works wonderfully. Since making it the first time, I've reduced the sugar to 1/3 cup and increased the cocoa to 4 tbsp. I also like it with more vanilla and double the salt but it isn't necessary. If you want to make a sturdier pudding like for pie or if you just want it decadent like me then you can add a couple egg yolks as well. Whisk them with a little milk and stir them in when the pudding starts to thicken. If you do that, be sure to hold (and stir) it at a boil for at least 90 seconds to neutralize an enzyme in the yolk that breaks down starch. Otherwise you'll have muddy puddles in your pudding.

text:
I had an entire gallon of milk that was about to expire, so decided to make some pudding to use it up.  Didn't have a lot of ingredients on hand, so used this recipe as a base with a few substitutions that I don't think impacted the overall result. Followed the recipe but substituted a slightly heaping 1/4 cup of chocolate chips for the cocoa powder and butter, and reduced the sugar to a heaping 1/4 cup.  I was really surprised at how good this tasted!  Taste was great, but gave it 4 stars for the consistency.  I think using cornstarch as the thickener causes the pudding to have a jelly-like consistency (It jiggles when you shake it, for example).  That's not what I think of when I think of pudding.  If you can look past that, the flavor and mouth texture are good.

text:
I have to comment on this one! Pudding sounds so simple, and this one is a snap to put together, but the flavors & smooth texture sets it apart. I make this at least once a week (or more). Only changes for personal taste, is I only use 1.5 Tablespoons cocoa (I know ... what??) but I prefer it to be a lighter chocolate flavor. I've also used brown & white sugar 1/4 c each. The key is to combine it as suggested, on the stove so you can whisk away while cooking it! Cook until it really coats the back of that spoon, mine usually lightly boils for 1 minute or so. Whisk the whole time. Add the butter & vanilla at the end and this is a winner!

I was interested in making pudding but didn't have any in a box.  Boy am I glad I didn't.  This is better than any boxed pudding and so worth the effort.  I read other reviews first.  So, I put all my dry ingredients in a bowl and stirred them all together, then added to the dry pan and stirred a bit till some of the sugar melted. I added 3/4 cup of milk to dry ingredients in pan and stirred with a slotted wooden spoon.  Once all the ingredients combined, I added the rest of the milk and stirred.. Wah-la. No lumps.

text:
I made this recipe as written with no substitutions or alterations and it came out just fine. The flavor and creamy consistency of the pudding is worth a solid four-plus stars but I gave it five stars overall because of the simplicity of the recipe, and I value simplicity especially when the results are this good. I used a whisk first to combine the dry ingredients and then to incorporate the milk until the mixture came to a boil. I finished cooking the pudding with a metal spoon so I could see how it coated the spoon, then used the whisk again to blend in the butter and vanilla. I used Hershey's "Special Dark" cocoa and while it was quite delicious, I agree with another reviewer who said this pudding is only as good as the cocoa. While I like Special Dark for making brownies, I'm eager to try this recipe again using a better quality cocoa. Update: I made this pudding with Droste (Dutch Processed Unsweetened Cocoa Powder) and the result was near perfection! Droste will be my "go to" cocoa from now on.

The ingredients had potential. However the result was something more like the thickness of mashed potatoes the next day. I agree with several of the other posters. There needs to be a cut down on the cornstarch - drastically. Also I saw no benefit of the butter. It never incorporated into the pudding and was just butter swimming in the mass of chocolate. The next day the butter was cooled and each to pick out since it just sit on top and to the sides. I would add the vanilla into the mixture as it was cooking if I ever try this recipe again.

None
text:
Great, easy recipe. We have people with a milk allergy in my family, so I substituted homemade coconut milk (just shredded coconut plus water in the blender for a few minutes) for the milk and coconut oil for the butter. It had a little bit of a coconut flavor that played nicely against the chocolate. 

I think I will use a little less cornstarch next time. Only use the amount in the recipe if you're going to put the pudding into the serving dishes while still warm. Once the pudding cools with this much cornstarch in it, it gels and won't spread at all when you spoon it into a bowl.

Oh my, this is sooooo good! I've never made homemade pudding before but now I'm glad that I did. Not only is it super easy to make, it tastes a hundred times better than store bought pudding. text:
This is the perfect chocolate pudding recipe!!! I loved it, and so did my husband who happens to be VERY picky about chocolate pudding! :)   The recipe is just fine as is, but in preparing it, I have a couple of tips:   - put the dry ingredient through a sifter before putting into the saucepan.  - after adding the milk, use the back of a spoon or silicone spatula to break up the lumps that will inevitably show up while cooking - whisk the entire time while cooking and bring to a boil  This is fantastic pudding to use in a pie, triffle, or just as an indulgent chocolate snack! LOVE IT!!!

text:
This is a wonderful basic recipe for chocolate pudding. The basic recipe can take a lot of modifications and still it still turns out great, as long as you keep the ratio of cornstarch to liquid constant.  I usually use 1/4 cup of sugar and 4 T of dark cocoa powder for richer chocolate flavor, and the consistency is always perfect.  I've also substituted coffee for part of the milk with great results.  The basic recipe can also be made dairy-free very easily. I've made it with almond milk, and it turned out great-it just needed an extra minute or two of cooking to thicken up.

text:
Great recipe! The key is starting all ingredients on low heat until everything has been added and mixed well. Increase heat - and stir constantly until it boils. Once it comes to a boil, set the timer for 1 minute stirring constantly. Once that is finished, remove from heat, and stir in butter and vanilla. You can cool or eat it warm, but it should gel up perfectly. Pro tip: Using a good quality milk pan makes all the difference.

text:
This was easy to make. I think it needs a little more cocoa in proportion to the amount of milk, so I added another tablespoon of cocoa. If one likes a richer chocolate flavor you could add one quarter cup of cocoa which I would do if making it for a pie and decrease the milk by about a half cup. Also, cook at medium heat and no more stirring constantly  until it comes to a boil, then continue cooking for another minute. It will start to thicken before it boils. Cool for two hours  and serve  with whip cream, or else, pour into a pie shell and refrigerate. Delicious!

text:
This recipe is divine!  I followed another reviewer's suggestion and added 1 additional tablespoon of cocoa (4 tablespoon total).  I also used arrowroot flour instead of cornstarch (a little less than 1/4 cup).  

Tossed the first 5 ingredients in a blender and blended for 30 seconds to lessen the chance of "clumps" during the heating process.

Next time I will use low heat the entire time and stir more to avoid burning.  Still super delicious and my family practically ate the whole pot!!

First time made as directed - let cook adequate time as suggested, loved it. Second time, put in cook crust topped with marshmallows and toasted under broiler 2.5 minutes. Told kids its a smores pie. Third time added 3 egg yolks, (whip, set aside, added hot pudding a few spoonfuls at a time, until brought up to temp then added to pot and cooked an additional few minutes.) Then I put it cupcakes with chocolate cookie crust on the bottom and again toasted marshmallows on top. Told kids it was hot cocoa cupcakes. They loved it every time. Great easy recipe.

text:
Excellent chocolate pudding. For those complaining that it's too thin it's pudding not pie filling so it will be thinner than maybe you're used to. Also, it needs to cook for at least 2 mins after it comes to a boil. Sometimes I use 1/4 cup white & 1/4 cup light brown sugar. Still tastes like great chocolate pudding but adds a little richness to the flavor. Or add a bit of cinnamon or instant coffee powder for that hint in the background that seems like an added bonus.

text:
This a very cheap, lovely and tasty option. Ive made this quite few times, and its nice. Nothing fancy, but it does the job. Here are some tips Ive got for you, they will make your job easier:

Instead of doing everything on the pan, mix your dry ingredients with 1 cup of milk and put the 1 1/3 on the stove to warm up. When the milk is warm add the chocolate water and this way you are less likely to get lumps and whatnot. Remember! Dont stop stirring. That is very important.

With every recipe I have tried on this sight, I first follow the recipe thoroughly. I try to rate each one based on the recipe itself. Then if I want to add or change anything I do that on my own. So, what I am trying to say is that when I rate a recipe with 5 stars it's because I loved it the way it is. As I read through reviews I get a little upset when recipes are rated low because someone decided to jack with the original. Do not rate a recipe poorly because you jacked up, blame yourself, not the recipe! I made this and it turned out fantastic and yes, next time I will put saran wrap over the top to prevent the strange "crust" from forming but other than that, this was perfect. Thank you so much for sharing this recipe.

text:
This is the perfect recipe if you are making a pie or dessert with filling!  I made my pudding with dark chocolate and 1/4 cup of extra sugar (brown) just because it is my family's preference.  I would suggest breaking up and lumps in the dry ingredients by hand before you add the milk.  You can also measure the cornstarch with a 1/4 cup of the milk and mix them well before adding them to the pot.  Then add the remaining 2 1/2 cups of milk.  Any lumps left should be fairly easy to crush on the side of the pan with a metal spoon  before the mixture starts to boil.  Thank you for the recipe!  It is a keeper.

text:
The end product was way to thin to eat as pudding, even after chilling overnight. It tasted great although I did make one small change to the recipe: I added marscapone to the cooked mixture, off the heat with the butter and vanilla which made it extra creamy. Instead of tossing the "pudding", I decided to fix it. I combined 1 1/2 C milk, 1/2 C corn starch and 1/2 C cocoa powder (it wasn't chocolatey enough for me) and cooked it until very thick (I thought it was already a bit too sweet so didn't add sugar. The finished pudding was sweet enough for me). I stirred in 2 T butter and 2 t vanilla and 2 T marscapone then let it chill. Much better!

text:
Very good and very smooth. As previous reviewers suggested, I used 1/2 c of light brown sugar instead of the white and it did make the flavor more rich tasting. I also followed the suggestion to use 3 heaping tablespoons of cocoa, which boosted the chocolate flavor and blended nicely with the brown sugar. Other than that, I followed the recipe. Made sure the dry ingredients were lump-free before whisking in the milk, then placed the pot on the stove. I whisked constantly while cooking, then when fully cooked removed from the heat and whisked in the butter and vanilla. Cooled by whisking the pot of pudding in a sink full of cold water before transferring to a bowl & covering the surface with plastic wrap and refrigerating. It was very creamy and "chocolatey". Family loved it.

https://images.media-allrecipes.com/userphotos/50x50/5614247.jpg
city:
None
region:
None
country:
None
text:
I've made this at least 3 times, and I have been very pleased.  The recipe doubles nicely, and that's a good thing, because if your family loves chocolate pudding as much as mine, you'll want more.  I was able to successfully tweak the recipe by replacing the white sugar with a sugar / stevia blend such as Truvia and the newer product called Zing, by using fat-free milk and by reducing the butter by one fourth.  The pudding tastes better the following day so if you can plan ahead, try to make it the day before you want it or need it.  Since the recipe calls for stirring constantly, I found that using a wire whisk works very nicely because it breaks up any clumps.   This is the perfect treat for when you are craving something sweet and creamy.  Thank you, Kelly Thompson, for such a wonderful recipe!

text:
I tried making it last night and ended up with the perfect texture (just like pudding), but totally ruined the taste by burning it (cooking it too fast; too high a heat) and adding too much salt.  I'm sure the garbage disposal loved it, tho... :-D

Tonight, I tried something different.  I used our Vitamix blender to blend all the ingredients together (made sure all were carefully measured out, including the salt), except the cornstarch.  I tasted it... tasted like good cocoa!  Poured it into the pan and heated it a bit before adding the cornstarch.  Tasted the spoon after it thickened up proper (Ouch! Burned my tongue!) and now it's cooling in the fridge.  I think I nailed it pretty well this time.  Pays to follow the instructions! :-D

I might be adding a little more cornstarch than the recipe asks for, which is possibly why it's coming out the proper consistency when done.  Someone commented it was kinda runny.  Might want to try cooking it a bit longer or adding a pinch more time (not thyme!  HA!).

Beats paying for the stuff on the shelf with artificial food colors.  That was my motivation for trying to make REAL chocolate pudding... and I'm a guy! :-D

text:
This pudding is fantastic! I can't get enough. My advice is you need to babysit while its heating. Don't let more than 30 seconds go by without stirring. When it starts to steam its getting close and once all the bubbles go away its done cooking after 30 seconds or so. That last part of the cook time is the most crucial. Don't let it lump up!  I also add 1/2 teaspoon of cornstarch just to tighten it up.

text:
Delicious! I made a few adjustments to the recipe and that's still a work in progress, but overall I'd say this recipe was a big WIN!

One thing I did was replace approximately half of the sugar with stevia sweetener (which I added after cooking). That worked out fine, but I'm not sure I got just the right amount of stevia. So, that will take a little more experimenting.

I added a teensy bit more cocoa (as I read others had done) and accidentally used 3 cups of milk instead of 2-3/4. I also added less than a Tablespoon of butter (because I'm worried about the fat content) but I think what I did add still enhanced the flavor.

It seemed obvious that the recipe would be perfect as-is, or you could do some small adjustments here and there and find success that way. I'll be cooking this again!

text:
I have made this 3 times now, and I LOVE it! I tried writing a review before and accidentally published it before I said why I like it so much :) I agree with kittypie when I say, use BROWN SUGAR, it makes the flavor much deeper and richer. Also if you don't want an usually thick jello type pudding with a strange texture, don't use all the cornstarch, only a little over half (which would be about 2 1/2 tablespoons) . I have done it different ways. The first time with less cornstarch and brown sugar and it was magnificent. The second time with all the cornstarch and it was, meh, ok I guess, would have been ok for a cake filling maybe but way way too thick. Third time I tried with white sugar as called for, and half plus a little of the cornstarch as I did the first time, it tastes very good but would be 20 times better with the brown sugar. Hope this helps! I know I always read reviews before I cook things from this site, I'm grateful for kittypie's suggestions, also, chopped almonds or fruit on top is very yummy! Happy cooking all!

text:
Excellent recipe!  I ran the cocoa, starch and sugar through a sieve.  I doubled the ingredients, (using half brown sugar and half granulated sugar) cooked over med hi, whisking fast and constantly (and forgot to add the salt) - so it quickly came to a boil.   Once I brought it to a boil,  I reduced the heat to simmer, whisked briskly as I cooked it 3 minutes longer.  Turned out perfectly!  Once transferring to serving dishes, I covered it with plastic wrap touching the surface to eliminate/remove the thick film that forms over the top when refrigerated.  This recipe is great for whipping up a quick and easy chocolate treat, for sure.    Simply impressive.  Everyone here loved it.  :)

city:

region:

country:

text:
YUM!  This was delicious - so much better than the boxed pudding... and better ingredients too.  This really didn't take long to make.  It was not lumpy at all for me and I didn't use a double boiler.  I whisked together the sugar, cornstarch, cocoa powder and salt in a medium saucepan and then added in just a little bit of the milk at first and whisked it together - it was almost a paste.  Once it was smooth, then I added in the rest of the milk and cooked over medium heat.  I didn't whisk vigorously, just enough to keep anything from sticking to the bottom.  Once it came to a boil, then I started whisking faster and just waited until it looked like it had thickened up well.  The whole process took only about 10  minutes for me.  I don't like pudding skin and I don't like putting plastic on top of anything hot, so I just transferred it to a serving bowl and left it on the counter top - whisking every few minutes until it started to cool, which kept any skin from forming.  I like pudding cold best, but I thought this was even good warm!  Great recipe, I will definitely be making this again.

text:
I love this pudding!!! 
I had read a review about the pudding being too thin but this is not true at all, Im thinking they didn't cook it long enough to get the right consistency. 

The first time I made it I followed the recipe exactly but after that I made a few modifications.

I skipped adding the sugar at the beginning and when the pudding was ready I added 6 individual packets of Twin sugar. I used almond milk instead of regular milk (since I don't drink regular milk) and I added only 1 tablespoon of butter ( I used margarine instead).

The pudding is rich and delicious!!  You must be patient when cooking puddings since they have to be stirred constantly . Boil and simmer until thick enough. It gets even thicker when cooled.

text:
I followed the recipe exactly and this turned out amazing! As I had seen from other reviewers that it was a bit thick and better for pie I poured mine into a crust and let it cool in the fridge, then topped with home made whipped cream. It was delicious and gone in two days. I was multitasking while making this so I definitely was not "stirring constantly" I think this may have been beneficial considering there weres also reviews stating it was too thin and soup like. Just make sure to boil it long enough to thicken up and don't go crazy with stirring it. Oh and I think if you're getting lumps of cocoa or corn starch in your pudding,  you need a sifter so you aren't pouring hard to break apart chunks of powder into the mix in the first place. 
My experience was great. Delicious chocolate pudding pie!

text:
This is what chocolate pudding is supposed to taste like. I make as directed except with 1/4 cup cocoa powder (equivalent to 4 tbsp). This is easy to tweak with fancy flavors if desired. For people who don't know how to use cornstarch, you MUST boil it for it to become clear and lose its floury taste, basic kitchen chemistry. The butter temperature seems unimportant (it just melts!) but there's a reason to add vanilla last; otherwise it would evaporate off and lose flavor in boiling.

text:
Excellent and straight forward recipe. To all those having problems with the viscosity, temperature and movement is key. Too much heat causes the starch to unwind onto itself and congeal/burn on the bottom. Too little heat will result in thin, chalky tasting pudding. Reduce liquid to a gentle simmer, stirring constantly for 2 to 3 min. It is also quite useful to thoroughly  dissolve the corn starch in the cold milk before applying heat. If you add more cocoa, reduce the amount of starch or increase the amount of liquid slightly as the cocoa will also serve to thicken the slurry. Simple recipes are easy to tweak.

text:
This is exactly the recipe I was looking for to taste like the boxed "cook & serve" stuff of my youth! I read through several reviews first, as I always find that helpful on this site, so I did incorporate some of those ideas for the good and bad on my first try. First off, I stuck with 1/4 C cornstarch as published and had no problems with consistency. I dropped sugar to 1/3 C as I always find American recipes too sweet. Upped salt to 1/4 tsp and also upped cocoa to 4 heaping teaspoons. I mixed 3 different types I had on hand: Hershey's special dark, Wilbur's and Bellagio sipping chocolate cocoa for extra decadence. I also threw in a few drops of hot sauce just for kicks although I didn't really taste it. The second batch I just made this morning was perfect! The difference between it and last week's was that last week I used 1 can of evaporated milk (per reviewer) along with whole milk, as I didn't have enough milk on hand. There was definitely an unpleasant, weird flavor last week that I attributed to the evaporated milk although I was concerned I might have slightly burned it too. So this week I used all whole raw milk and noticed none of the weirdness even though I had some slightly burnt stuff stuck on the bottom of the pot again. So unless you really like the flavor of evaporated milk, I would not suggest it for this recipe. As for the skin, I like it as proof it's homemade pudding

country:

text:
If you add 1 T cornstarch to 1c liquid, bring it to a boil & boil for 1 minute, you got jel!!  Works for pudding, gravy, fruit goo for pies, etc.  This recipe has 4T (1/4 c) cornstarch to 2 3/4 c milk.  If you bring this to a boil & hold for 1 min it cannot help but thicken! I know that ultra pasturized milk is no good for cheese as it will not curd.  Perhaps this may be part of the 'not thickening' problem.  I used "dutched" cocoa (Droste's) & will try again with a non dutched like Hershey's just to compare.  The Droste's was delicious.  Plenty of chocolatey flavor for me.  To the guy who made this & said it tasted like broccoli... the off flavor may have come from your butter, your pan or your cocoa.  If you follow the recipe with fresh, tasty ingredients, I guarantee it will NOT taste like broccoli.  Maybe it will if you burn it.

text:
This was lovely!  I'm trying to cook healthier, less processed things for my family, and this was the perfect alternative to chemical artificial colorings, additives, and preservatives in a box.

I stirred the dry ingredients with a whisk while adding the milk, while the pan was on medium heat.  When everything looked smooth and clump-free, I increased the heat to high, and it thickened right up before it even came to a boil. I added the butter and vanilla and stirred until it incorporated.  I put the pudding in 4 individual serving bowls and put them in the fridge.  Half an hour later it had set up to the perfect consistency.  It did have the skin on top, I did not cover it, but I like it that way.  Husband and 2 teenaged boys said it was great.  Thank you for a healthier option!

text:
Thank you for posting this recipe! It replicates the "cornstarch pudding" my mom used to make "by feel" (without a recipe) on Sunday evenings. She died suddenly a few years ago, and until I discovered this recipe, I hadn't been successful in finding a similar-tasting, easy (foolproof, even!) version of this type of home style cooked pudding. I've made it several times and have been happy with the results every timeregardless of whether I used whole milk, one, or two percent (it just depends what I have in the refrigerator). One suggestion for anyone who prefers thick(er) pudding: after bringing the mixture to a,full boil, just continue stirring constantly for a minute or two longer. You will see and feel the difference in the texture, and it will continue to thicken as it cools.

text:
So delicious! This was very easy to make. I followed the recipe, except I left out the butter (I didn't think it was necessary.) I did used 1/2% milk. This was so wonderful. It turned out perfectly. I will certainly make this again. Next time, I might try to cut back the cornstarch and the sugar (it was really sweet; not a bad thing at all, but I might try to make it a little "healthier"). Also, I would recommend covering the pudding with plastic wrap right on the surface of the pudding if you refrigerate any. If not covered this way, it will have a thick skin (which some people may not like.) This pudding is so good nice and cold, right from the fridge. Thank you, Kelly, for this yummy recipe!

I would have given this five stars execpt for one problem. The recipe says let it boil, some viewers say dont let it boil. I've found that letting it boil is let important than how much it thickens up while it's on the heat. When it gets to a syrupy consistancy and thickly coats the back of the spoon, then remove it from heat, whether it's boiled or not.

This is really 2-1/2 star pudding.  I love the flavor, simplicity and quick prep, but it is very thin.  I refrigerated it, and it just separated. text:
Maybe it's because I use whole milk, but the first couple times I made the recipe it came out too thick & gelatinous for my liking. However, with a few modifications, this is the BEST chocolate pudding I have ever eaten! I add an extra tablespoon of chocolate and cut the cornstarch in half to 1/8 of a cup and it comes out rich, smooth, amazing. Cutting the cornstarch in half makes softer & creamier, very similar to the texture of "instant" pudding (which I like). I have good results using a wire whisk (no lumps) and then refrigerating it overnight before serving. Thanks so much for posting!

I think this would be perfect as the recipe states rather than altering it by reducing the cornstarch. Will try again as is written.

text:
As I was gathering the ingredients for the pudding I realized I had a rolled pie crust and some heavy cream in the refrigerator, so I decided to make a chocolate cream pie.  The pudding for the filling turned out to be very good, but I didn't really get any comments on the finished pie.  The consistency of the pudding was stiff enough that it kept its shape when slices of the pie were cut.  I think this would probably be better as just pudding, since the crust and whipped cream seemed to cut down on the chocolate flavor.
